< Text>
I've passed through here for many years without any problems.  Typical delay time is 15 minutes but can vary from a couple of minutes to as much as an hour (my longest delay).  I recommend lowering all your vehicle windows when you're one or two cars before going thru inspection.  Officers appreciate getting a clear view of the car interior and its occupants.  I usually get waved to proceed right on through without any further questions, and I've never been asked to go to a secondary inspection. Also, try to have your ID/passport, or docs in your hand ready to present.  Officers rarely ask questions if you quickly show them your ID documents.</Text>

<Review>I've come here several times so I should probably finally review it since it obviously keeps me coming back for more. I've had lunch here a lot but this was my first time trying it for breakfast. Unfortunately for me it was so good my wallet will be very unhappy because I might come back here for breakfast everyday.
I got the Korean Pork Breakfast Burrito and it was incredible. I love breakfast burritos, and I love Korean BBQ, but I never considered combining them before. I'm so glad this place did that because the spicy pork with egg and mozzarella wrapped up in a tortilla was mouth watering. I ate it very slowly to savor and each bite was better than the last as I dread the final bite which meant the end of my delicious journey. I can't wait to go back and get it again!< /Review><Gmap_id>0x80dd2a13faa6286d:0xb56f5f853ba47c6f< /Gmap_id>< user>

< text>
I was recently in Palo Alto for a big birthday celebration and needed a nice, clean, inexpensive place to sleep. After looking online, this seemed to be the best bet. It didn't disappoint. My room was clean, comfortable, and had everything I needed (e.g., coffee pot, ironing board, free wireless internet, refrigerator). Parking (at no charge) was convenient, breakfast (also included) was hot (e.g., excellent Belgian waffles), USA Today was free in the lobby, and the maids, breakfast staff, and front desk people were friendly and very helpful. It was perfect for what I needed, and I highly recommend it.<//text>

This Comfort Inn is my first choice when staying in the Palo Alto area, about six time a year. The rooms are clean, the beds and pillows are very comfortable, and I love the "home" comforts in the room - coffee maker, frig, microwave. The continental breakfast is very convenient as well.
It would be nice to have an exercise facility, or access to one.
I do compare rates, and this generally has the most competitive rate for the area for the quality of stay.
But I give my highest ratings to the staff. Denise and her staff have always been helpful and friendly. If there's something missed, or if I have suggestion for improving the convenience in a room, they address it right away, and always show appreciation for having it brought to their attention so they can improve.
Denise has helped in several ways to make my experiences with this Comfort Inn very positive!<//review>

<Text>First of all, the front desk lady who apparently answered my call was unnecessarily rude and cold.

I booked on a wrong date by mistake and understood that I'd not get my money back but the way she handled my call was so cold and rude. She said, "no we can't change your reservation and absolutely no refund. go ahead and dispute if you wish"

< review>
I found this Comfort Inn to be a reasonable place to stay. The bed was quite comfortable and the breakfast items available were reasonable. Staff was easy to approach and interact with. <UserId.>109330532107896316978</UserId.><username>Jessica Dial</username><Date>1545192585094< /Date><Rate>4< /Rate>< Text>
The hotel isn't bad at all. Room was clean and bed was comfy. My complaints are merely that the toilet runs non stop (refill valve leaks causing tank water to overflow the water line and run into bowl), and the fridge door is offset causing it to have a leaky seal which results in frozen food that I merely wanted chilled and not icey. Loved that the showerhead is one of the handheld ones with a hose, and the fact that there were cotton balls and q-tips provided in the room. Overall, it is a very nice comfort inn, and the minor annoyances I experienced are probably room specific and not a hotel wide issue. Would stay here again.</Text>

< Text>
The Comfort Inn is a relatively inexpensive establishment for the area. The rooms are relatively spacious but could use some upgrades. A little mold in the shower, a chair that looks like it definitely should not be in the room because of stains and age, a little wallpaper peeling off the walls. The rooms were relatively clean and the beds were a little soft but the pillows were good. It has a nice TV and charging station for your electronics next to the bed which is very convenient. There is no closet in the room but they do have a a small armoire to hang your clothing. Overall I would say that it is a good value for this area.<//Text>

<Rate>None</Rate>< Text>
I have been staying at the Comfort Inn in Palo Alto for several years, my husband is a patient at Stanford Hospital. While the hotel is certainly not a high end hotel it does serve the need of what we need while in Palo Alto for appointments. It is always clean and comfortable, the staff always friendly.
I am always surprised, however, at the increase in pricing, I do realize that demand for accomadations, location and competition have a big influence in the costs. I sometimes feel the increase is unreasonable. I do realize if I pay in advance I can reduce the price, although there are times when medical appointments must be changed. Unfortunately, your pre pay option does not allow for changes in reservations.< /Text>

<Gmap_id>0x808fba62028d118d:0x6f31c15be66eff25< /Gmap_id><UserId.>None< /UserId.><rating>None</rating><Review>The rooms were very nice, clean and looked newly remodeled, especially the bathroom. The rooms are a bit small but this is a busy city area with tight real estate. I'm more used to small town and wide open suburbs. But they made good use of the space in the room and it was very nice. We had a room in the very back facing away from the parking lot and that made us a little nervous especially arriving very late on the first night. But it turns out that it is fenced and backs up to the playground of a child care center so it was very quiet in the evenings and weekends. We never felt concerned for our safety. There was enough parking even on the nights that there was no vacancy. The breakfast was fair being a standard Comfort Inn breakfast. The waffle maker seemed to be having problems, it never got quite hot enough to cook the waffles enough inside. The staff was excellent. I broke my reservation up into 3 to use points on the nights that were more expensive. The night clerk went ahead and checked me in on all 3 reservations that first night and we didn't have to do anything more after that. If you have points, make sure you pay attention to the nightly rates. The mid-week rates are more than twice the rate of the weekend nights but the points are the same for any night. It was well worth it to use points on the weeknights.</Review></record>

Clean rooms, but leaves a lot to be desired
1. It's conveniently located
2. Rooms are clean and have basic amenities shown on their website
3.  Staff though courteous they keep referring queries to their manager
4.  Also there seem to be a lot of disconnect between the property team and the central choice team. Eg. Out of the blue I was told that city tax is increased by 1.5percent..on asking why I wasn't informed upfront they said they didn't know it.  Such city changes don't happen overnight... They finally adjusted this amount, but communication gap is clearly visible.
5. Breakfast is good. Though menu remains exactly the same all days they have a decent spread much Better than the grab and go bfast options in this area.
6. My Visa forex credit card didn't work at their place and the reason given was their payment gateway doesn't accept it.  .this same card  works all through america...I had to pay by cash....that's quite some inconvenience and the team need to really sort it out with most out of country travellers adopting the  forex card
Overall decent place. Clean and good for a shirt stay</review>

<Text>I just had the front windshield on my 2012 M3 replaced by Safelite.  I am totally satisfied with the work.   This is unusual for me. I am not easily impressed.

Walter (Pasadena @ Hill and Walnut) did it at my home. Walter is a great tech. He was super meticulous, polite, professional and most important, he treated my car as if it were his own.  I highly recommend if you want the best, ask for him.

Some background follows -  My car is a garage queen which I ordered to my spec, waited 5 months for and bought new and plan to keep forever.

It has never been valet parked, crashed (almost the same result as being valet parked) or driven in the rain. I am super concerned with who touches it or works on it.  I do all my own maintenance as I do not trust others to not do more harm than good.

I requested and paid extra (about twice the cost of the online Safelite quote for non-oem glass) for actual factory OEM glass with the BMW logo on it - just because.

My Stealership quoted me 3.8x what safelite charged. Another Stealer quoted 3x.  A very highly rated independent BMW shop quoted around 2.6x and would have done a very good job as well.

In the end, I took a chance with Safelite and it paid off. Not only were they much more affordable, they offer a lifetime warrantee as well. They took photos of any dings or scratches on the car (almost none so far) and had me sign off on that. They put protective tape where needed. Installed heavy vinyl seat covers to protect my pristine leather. They used heavy fender protectors as well as a full sized engine blanket for when the hood was open.  They even put a steering wheel protector on.  This care was very important to me.

One more thing. It has come to my attention that the Stealers do not do  glass replacements in-house and likely use whoever is cheapest so there is nothing to be gained by paying them through the nose for this work.

The jury is still out regarding if OEM glass is worth it or not. For my car, I was happy to pay extra so the car looks totally original in stock condition. For my domestic SUV and pickup, I would gladly accept any decent manufacturer as long as it was a recognized brand with the proper options (tints, auto wiper sensors etc).

Five stars!  Ask for Walter and you will not be disappointed.< /Text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPArAN3TkxmgWAIVAj4jZXwMxBpa374WLFwLdlm=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< resp>

Got a small crack on the corner right of my 2018 Toyota Prius, within 2 days, it spread quick. Call GEICO, my insurance and Safelite in Pasadena was their choice for me.

Their price appears to be fair. GEICO doesn't do OEM, only aftermarket parts and so far I have no issues as of yet. OEM would of cost me $1,800, aftermarket was about under $600 (parts and labor).

I wish this new manager and crew the best and hope they will continue to provide the best service they can and make Pasadena proud and #1 in SoCal.< /Text>

<user>101639272871426856304</user>< Name>
Mike Hua</Name>
<date>1526452020243< /date><rating>2< /rating>< Review>
I was in town looking for a Chinese lunch spot. Upon arrival, the wait was conspicuously long, but decided to wait because the soup dumplings looked really appetizing. When getting seated after 30 minutes, I realized that the restaurant was severely understaffed not only outside the kitchen but also inside as well for a Sunday noon service. Long story short, we put order in for 4 dishes but only ate 2 because they simply couldn't turn around the remaining 2 dishes within 20 minutes of serving the first two. The waiter was nice enough to explain the under-staffing situation, but assessing the situation at the time, we suspected even another 20 minutes wouldn't be enough.

On to the review of the dishes. The soup dumplings were actually not bad. I could tell they were freshly made and the dough skins were made very thin and chewy, just the way I like them. The fillings were fairly soupy and the soup was light and flavorful, but not too oily. Although they executed this dish very well, I was heavily disappointed in the other two dishes. The smoke fish was one of the worst I've had because it was clear to me that the dish was made a while ago - too cold even for a cold dish - and the execution was rather poor. The fish tasted extremely bland even when I smothered them in sauce. I always enjoyed eating this dish growing up because the father-side of my family always prepared this dish. It really bothered me that they completely butchered this dish. Finally, the soy milk with Chinese You-Tiao is at best mediocre because they've managed over-soak the You-Tiao to the point it was falling apart. All in all, if I were to return again, probably will just stick to the safe dishes like the soup dumplings.</Review>

< user_name>
Cecilia Knapp<//user_name>
< Time>
1577685477801< /Time>
< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< text>
It's just ok, I've definitely had better dumplings at other places. My friend, who is vegetarian, brought me, my brother, and nephew here to try. She said her non-vegetarian friend really liked it and she at least has some options. We had an order of the pork XLB, pork pan-fried dumplings, green onion pancake, vegetarian potstickers, and stir-fried rice cakes. These are all items I've had at other places and I was underwhelmed. The wrapper on the XLB were too thick, though our order did come out nice and hot. There was a good amount of broth and the taste of the pork was good, the wrapper was just way too thick and doughy. Same with the pan-fried dumplings - they were almost as thick and doughy as steamed pork buns that you'd get a dim sum, but with the little pork meatball inside. The green onion pancakes were fried nice and golden and had a good taste, they just weren't flakey layers like I'm used to, but at least they were not oily. I didn't try the vegetarian potstickers but they did erroneously give us pork ones at first which my vegetarian friend found out after she bit into one. The rice cakes were ok, nothing extra special about them.

It was easy to find street parking and walk right in to get a table for 4 at 6:30 on a Sunday, but I don't know that I'm ever planning to go back.<//text>

Cindy Toh</username>

1457935253890< /date>
<Rating>4</Rating>< review>
Authentic Chinese food. Yummy dumplings!

Came by on a Sunday evening for dinner. There was a line outside the restaurant, we waited for approx 15mins before we were seated.

We were promptly served with tea and shortly after, a server came by to take our orders. We ordered Hot and Sour soup (3/5), Shanghai Dumplings (4/5), buns with condensed milk (4/5) and Beef with capsicum (3/5).

I had wanted to order their savory soy bean milk, unfortunately they are only available for breakfast/lunch.

The portions were huge for each of the dishes, enough for 3-4 to share. It was two of us so we ended up packing quite a bit of food home.

Overall, the food are authentic and tasty. Typical Chinese restaurants are really noisy, this was manageable.

Will be back again.< /review>

< review>
I went here on our search for shanghai Dumplings.  I've got to say, that these were some of the best that I've had in the Bay Area.  They had a tasty flavor and there was actually soup in most of the dumplings.

As for the restaurant itself, it is not a flashy store front located right on Broadway in Millbrae.  We were asked to put our name on a list when we arrived even though there was a large number of open tables.  We were seated quite quickly, but the service was somewhat rushed and when we tried to get our waiters attention for either a glass of cold water or our bill, it was quite tough to gain his attention.

Would I go back despite the service, sure!<//review>

<Review>I went with 3 other people around 1pm on a Sunday and waited almost 1/2 an hour to get a table, with 5 people ahead of me when we signed up. We quickly ordered and the food came out quickly. We ordered the 1) Shanghai Steamed Dumplings (XLB) ($9.95), 7) Spicy Wontons ($6.95), 8) Beijing Style Boiled Chives Dumpling ($6.95) and 172) Shanghai Pan Fried Noodles ($9.95). The best out of the items were the XLB, for sure. There was plenty of soup inside and it was really flavorful. That and the Chives dumplings come with a small bowl of vinegar. Dunno if they messed up the order of spicy wontons, but it was peanut flavor with no spice either...

Would I come back? Only if I'm in the neighborhood...<//Review>< gmapID>

<user>102943420172311872097</user><user_name>Mike Shaheen<//user_name><Time>1478719406574<//Time>< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Text>
As a newcomer 3 years ago to "real" Chinese food (you other midwest transplants probably know what I'm talking about) I made it my quest to try xiao long bao (the steamed dumplings with pork & soup) at every Shanghainese restaurant that offered it.

My wife's is Cantonese and grew up in the bay area with a restaraunt loving family, so over the years I have collected a list of dumpling rating criteria.

The ratios are arguably the most important criteria  to me.  If there is too little soup, there is less flavor.  If the dumpling is too thick, it can mask the flavor.  If there is not enough pork...well you see where I'm going with this.

Other xiao long bao issues:
- Served in a tiny foil tin that almost invariably sticks to dumpling
- Very salty broth
- Tough and/or dense port

This is turning into a food theory post, so I'll get to the point.

The Shanghai Dumpling Shop consistently serves delicious Xiao Long Bao.  I know the ratios preference is matter of opinion and maybe you like really salty soup, but I think these are the BEST.

And, maybe the highest praise I can offer in our hyper-critical Bay Area dining market:  "I have never heard anyone say anything bad about these wonderful dumplings."< /Text>

<rate>3< /rate><review>I had dinner here with a few friends, and it wasn't bad. After a brief wait, we were seated inside, and our waitress was surprisingly nice. She was more warm and welcoming than what you'd expect from typical Chinese service. Our food came pretty fast, too. Yay.

Stir Fried Pea Sprouts with Garlic - I liked the strong garlic flavor, but some of the pea sprouts were stiff around the stalks. The flavor wasn't bad, but the quality could've been better.

Stir Fried Rice Cakes - Mushy. Some pieces kept sticking to my teeth, which was annoying. They tasted pretty savory, but some more wok hei would've been better. I should mention that I'm not a super big fan of rice cakes, so I'm a little biased here.

Shanghai Stir Fried Noodles - Pretty good. The noodles had a tender, smooth bite that I liked. They had a savory flavor like the rice cakes but with a more enjoyable texture.

XLB - The skins were thin and broke open smoothly. There was a healthy amount of broth inside, and it had a very slight bitterness that reminded me of ginseng. Although I liked that part, I still thought it could've been more aromatic. More ginger and green onions would've made the flavors pop out more. The texture of the pork stuffing was a little on the gritty side, too. Still, the XLB weren't bad, but I wouldn't go out of my way to come here.</review>< name>
Nei Ng<//name>

<Time>1374420214962</Time><gmap_id>0x808f77a45cc3c221:0x1be4920351b20539</gmap_id><username>Nancy Sequoia</username>< text>
Recommend this place. You can find many traditional and common Chinese entrees here, including homestyle entrees and Chinese street food, e.g., sweet soy milk and Chinese donut. They also make great Chinese donuts and crab meat xiao long bao. Their food is authentic Chinese and overall well-made and delicious. However, as with many casual Chinese restaurants, there isn't much in terms of food presentation. The service is fast and friendly. In terms of decor and ambiance, this is not a hole-in the-wall joint, but the place needs updated chairs and renovation. Because of the delicious food, this place can get crowded, lending to a lively atmosphere. Overall a great and enjoyable eating experience lending a little bit of nostalgia for those of us who enjoyed Chinese street food growing up.< /text>
